Ministry of Education Approves Zhejiang Province's Outline for Teacher Training 86

The Ministry of Education previously received the Zhejiang Education Department's report on the regulations and bibliography of the Teacher Training and Research Department, which was generally in line with the requirements. The ministry has instructed that they be filed for record, and hopes to report the organizational overview of the research department. It is said that the Zhejiang Provincial Teacher Training Communication and Research Department's organizational outline has been submitted to the ministry, and the ministry has now designated the department to approve it for record. The outline is recorded on the left

Organizational Outline of the Zhejiang Provincial Teacher Training Communication and Research Department Article 1 This outline is based on Article 2 of the regulations of the Zhejiang Provincial Teacher Training Communication and Research Department. The headquarters is composed of one director, one chief officer, one department officer, and several instructors. Article 3 The director of the headquarters is appointed by the director of the Department of Education. The chief officer, department officer, and instructors are designated by the director from the staff of the department. Article 4 The duties of the officers of the headquarters are divided as follows: "The director is responsible for supervising and directing all matters of the headquarters," "The chief officer handles the department affairs under the direction of the director and is responsible for guiding the students," "The department officer manages the receipt and dispatch of letters and the registration of various matters of the headquarters," "The instructor is responsible for answering the questions raised by the students of the headquarters and assessing the students' grades," Article 5 There is no fixed schedule for meetings of the headquarters. When necessary, the director will convene them at any time. Article 6 The expenses of the headquarters will be paid by the provincial government. Article 7 This outline will be implemented with the approval of the director of the Department of Education.

Preparatory Committee of the Chinese Marine Research Institute 87

The Chinese Marine Research Institute was established in Qingdao this summer. On the 17th of this month, the second congress was held at the Academia Sinica in the capital. Those present included Cai Yuanpei, Li Shizeng, Yi Peiji, Zhu Kezhen, Chen Shaokuan, Jiang Menglin, Yang Xingfo, and Song Chunfang. The following resolutions were made:

1. Expenses: Mr. Song Chunfang reported that the preparatory plan of the Chinese Marine Research Institute is divided into three major phases. The first phase is construction: (1) aquarium, (2) marine museum, (3) marine library. The first congress had decided to set up an aquarium in Qingdao first. The budget for its construction and start-up costs is 20,000 yuan, of which 10,000 yuan will be borne by the local agencies in Qingdao: 5,000 yuan by the municipal government, 3,000 yuan by the Qingdao Observatory, 1,000 yuan by Qingdao University, and 1,000 yuan by Mr. Song Chunfang himself through fundraising. The remaining 10,000 yuan will be borne separately by other academic institutions in China, such as the Academia Sinica, and various administrative agencies related to oceanography itself, such as the Navy Department, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining, and the Ministry of Education. Since the representatives of the various ministries and departments are present today, please decide on the allocation method of this 10,000 yuan. As for the construction of the aquarium, its appearance will be in the shape of a Chinese city wall. A gate tower will be built on the gate of the museum, which will be quite representative of the inherent architectural spirit of China. At present, the preparatory work is temporarily undertaken by the staff of the Marine Science Department of the Qingdao Observatory, which is completely voluntary, so there are no various expenses. It was decided that the following ministries and departments would each bear 2,000 yuan: (1) Academia Sinica (2) Peiping Research Institute (3) Navy Department (4) Ministry of Education (5) Ministry of Industry and Commerce (Minister Kong was absent due to illness) (6) Ministry of Agriculture and Mining will pay in four installments, 500 yuan per installment, from the end of October to the end of January of the 20th year, and the Ministry of Education will collect the money on its behalf (2) Mr. Zhu Kezhen proposed to change the name of the institute. Mr. Li Shizeng said that it is better to use the old name. Now the interest of the knowledge class in various places in the study of oceanography has gradually become stronger. For example, this autumn, someone in Beidaihe also proposed to set up a marine research institute. After the marine research institutes in various places are established in turn, each will be prefixed with the name of the place, such as Qingdao Chinese Marine Research Institute, Beidaihe Marine Research Institute, etc., and then "divide and combine" to become a systematic academic institution. (3) Mr. Song Chunfang proposed to increase the number of members of the committee. It was decided that the number of members of the committee would be increased from fifteen to nineteen. (4) Liu Hongsheng, Song Wusheng, Zheng Hongnian, and Gao Lu were publicly elected as preparatory members of the association.

Verification of Party Principles Knowledge Among Municipal School Staff 89

Various Measures Have Been Formulated and Promulgated

The Scope of Verification is Limited to the Three Principles of the People

The Municipal Party Department's Training Department is conducting an assessment of the knowledge of Party principles among faculty and staff in the city's primary and secondary schools, based on regulations issued by the Central Training Department. This was reported yesterday. A review of the "Brief Rules for Verifying the Study of Party Principles Among Faculty and Staff in Shanghai Municipal Primary and Secondary Schools," as formulated by the department, reveals that the verification is divided into three phases. The first phase, scheduled to begin next month, is limited to municipal primary and secondary schools. Regarding the scope of the verification, it was originally intended to follow the study program, with the first phase covering materials (i.e., Sun Wen's Doctrines, Military Spirit Education, and the Three Principles of the People). However, according to reports from various schools, most have not yet completed their studies. Therefore, it has been decided to first verify the Three Principles of the People, and then proceed to other books later. It is reported that notices and the "Brief Rules" have already been fully issued by the Municipal Training Department and forwarded to the Municipal Education Bureau, instructing all schools to prepare accordingly. The original text of the "Brief Rules" and "Instructions" are transcribed below:

Brief Rules for Verification (1) These rules are formulated in accordance with Article 3, Section 2 of the Central Training Department's "Rules for Assessing the Study of Party Principles Among Faculty and Staff at All Levels of Schools." (2) Party principle verification for schools at all levels will be conducted by personnel dispatched by the Municipal Training Department. The school principal, dean of students, and Party principle teachers shall be jointly responsible for assisting and supervising. (3) The verification will be conducted in three phases. The first phase will be for municipal primary and secondary schools, the second phase for registered primary and secondary schools, and the third phase for unregistered private primary and secondary schools. (4) The scope of the verification is divided into three rounds. The first round will cover the Three Principles of the People, the second round will cover the Outline of National Reconstruction, declarations and resolutions of past representative conferences, and the third round will cover the Strategies for National Reconstruction. (5) The term "faculty and staff" as used in these rules includes everyone from the principal to office staff. (6) Faculty and staff of all schools shall not be absent from the verification without a valid reason. (7) Part-time faculty and staff only need to undergo verification at one school. However, those who hold positions in both unregistered private schools and registered private schools should be verified by the registered school. Those who hold positions in both registered schools and municipal schools should be verified by the municipal school. Those who have already undergone verification at School A can declare this at School B and be exempt from verification. (8) The schedule for verification at each school will be arranged by the Municipal Training Department and notified to the school principal seven days in advance. Upon receiving the notice, the principal shall immediately inform all faculty and staff to prepare. (9) The verification time is set at half an hour. All those undergoing verification must submit their papers within the prescribed time limit and strictly adhere to all rules for standard testing. (10) After the verification is completed at each school, the Municipal Training Department will notify each school of its average score, as determined through review. Those with exceptionally high or low scores will be reported to the Municipal Education Bureau for separate rewards or penalties. (11) The dates and times of the verification will be announced separately by the Municipal Training Department. (12) These rules will be promulgated and implemented by the Municipal Training Department.

Instructions for Verification (1) The Shanghai Municipal Party Department's Training Department is conducting the first Party principle verification in accordance with Article 2, Section 2 of the Central Training Department's "Rules for Assessing the Study of Party Principles Among Faculty and Staff at All Levels of Schools." (2) The first verification is limited to faculty and staff of municipal middle schools in the city, with the Three Principles of the People as the scope of verification. (3) All faculty and staff of municipal schools in the city, from the principal to the office staff, must undergo the verification. Those who are unable to attend should state their reasons and request leave from the principal. (4) The date of the verification will be notified separately by the Municipal Training Department to each school seven days in advance. The time will be, in principle, 4:30 PM. (5) The verification time is limited to half an hour, and papers must be submitted when the time is up. (6) The school principal, dean of students, and Party principle teachers should be responsible for assisting and supervising during the verification. (7) After the verification is completed, the school principal or Party principle teacher should fill out a report form, stating the original number of participants, the number of absentees, the names of the absentees, and the reasons for their absence, and submit it along with the verification papers to the verification officer for return. (8) The verification officer is responsible for distributing and collecting the papers, as well as maintaining order, and has no authority to interpret questions. (9) If those undergoing verification have any questions about the verification questions, they should fill out a separate query form and submit it to the verification officer for return. The Municipal Training Department will provide a separate written reply or explanation. (10) The verification officer will record the spirit and discipline during the verification at each school and report it back to the department. (11) The quality of Party principle studies will be judged based on the verification scores of those undergoing verification and their spirit and discipline during the verification. (12) The number of absentees and attendees at each school, as well as the quality of order during the verification, will be the standard for each school's spirit and discipline in the study of Party principles. (13) The quality of spirit and discipline at each school will be the standard for evaluating the performance of the school principal and Party principle teachers. (14)

After the verification is completed, the Municipal Training Department will review the results according to the standards and notify each school. Those with exceptionally good or poor results will be reported to the Municipal Education Bureau for separate rewards or penalties.

A New Atmosphere at Datong University 94

Datong University has purchased many acres of land next to Zhongshan Road in Fan Wudu, west of Shanghai, to build a large-scale new dormitory. The land was purchased from the owners at a fair price, following the usual practice of real estate purchases by merchants and civilians. Enthusiastic people who are willing to donate their private land are also numerous, such as Qiao Hongzeng, Li Tixian, and Rong Zongjing, who have generously donated real estate to the school to show their support. Since the school moved in the autumn, the atmosphere has been refreshed, and the school's affairs have become increasingly developed. The number of students has surged. Recently, shops have sprung up in front of the school, and vehicles gather in crowds. The once-desolate area has suddenly become a bustling market, which has greatly benefited the nearby villagers.

Shanghai Guangzhao Girls' Elementary School was founded in the autumn of the 18th year of the Republic of China as a complete elementary school with an attached kindergarten and a girls' civilian night school. Huang Sheng-bai Goes to Japan for Research 96

Huang Sheng-bai, a native of Fujian, studied in Japan and the United States in his early years and obtained a Master of Agriculture degree from the University of Chicago in the United States. He is proficient in several languages, has a sturdy physique, and a calm demeanor. In the seventh year of the Republic of China, he crossed the sea from Guangdong, traveling alone with a suitcase across Qiong, Ya, Dian, Tibetan, Burmese, Indian, Siamese, Malay, and various islands in Southeast Asia for more than ten years, traveling tens of thousands of miles, to deeply investigate the realms of the Miao, Yao, Li, Tong, Guoguo, Kang Tibetan, and Malay peoples. He studied their lives, handled their totems, compared their dialects, and rubbed the broken steles and monuments of the Mojia, always recording what he had learned in volumes over a foot high. He recently went to Japan for research.

(3) Contingency Measures for Matches Canceled Due to Rain

The Shanghai Westerners' Football Association has many teams participating in the annual Group A matches and various cup competitions this season, so the schedule for Saturdays and Sundays is very crowded, and this will continue until the end of the football season. However, if matches are canceled due to rain and wet conditions, the schedule arranged by the football association will be completely disrupted, so it is necessary to plan for contingencies. It is now proposed that among the participating teams, those whose players do not work in business can be called together at any time during the week to reduce the congestion on weekends. However, notice must be given one week in advance. This method can be applied to the following teams: British Navy, Howards, Huaseisi, Westerners' Catch Health Team, RASC Twelfth Column, Italian Navy, French Army, Hujiang, St. John's, Red Hat, Sakol, Tongwen, Arrow Team, Headquarters Team, and Zhendan.

Recent Rice Prices Have Fallen Again 105

Japanese Rice Difficult to Sell

In the past two days, the amount of rice arriving has been unusually abundant. The highest price of new japonica rice is only about 15 yuan and 50 cents per stone, and new Songjiang rice is only 14 yuan. As for the amount of Japanese rice arriving, it is said that it has been transported in four or five batches, totaling more than 32,000 bags. A very small number of bags were taken out of the warehouse a few days ago, but now it has been stalled for several days, and even sample rice is being rejected. The situation of sales can be seen here.

Urging Active Preparations for Grain Storage Today 106

The Shanghai County Government received instructions from the Department of Civil Affairs yesterday, stating: In order to comply with the matter, the Provincial Government's 6335th instruction states: "In accordance with the Ministry of Interior's consultation, the preparation of grain storage is an important policy for preparing for famine and providing relief to the poor. The Ministry previously presented and approved the promulgation of the 'Local Granary Management Rules' in January of the 19th year, which was repeatedly consulted to the provinces, urging all counties, districts, townships, and towns to set up granaries to maintain the people's food supply. In the case, for half a year, according to the information reported by the provinces, most of the old Changping and other granaries in the counties have either collapsed and no longer exist, or have been moved for other purposes. The community granaries and charity granaries that were previously run in the villages have also been suspended for a long time and cannot be rebuilt. Even if a small number of counties have warehouses and factories, the remaining warehouse funds have mostly been used up, making it difficult to organize. Now, at the time of autumn harvest, most provinces have had a bumper harvest, and we should take this opportunity to carefully reorganize the original granaries in various places in accordance with the above rules. Those who have no granaries should actively prepare them to provide relief. On the one hand, the government should allocate public funds and store as much new grain as possible to prevent poor farmers from selling their grain at low prices due to livelihood pressures, resulting in low grain prices harming farmers. In addition to consulting separately, it is also necessary to consult the provincial government to examine and, in accordance with the Ministry's document of September 16 this year, instruct its subordinates to handle the matter together." This case was previously submitted to the Provincial Government for forwarding to the Yuan Ling, which ordered all counties to comply immediately, allocate warehouse funds, and store grain. If there are no existing funds, or if the funds are insufficient, measures should also be taken to borrow and purchase warehouses, and guarantees should be made. The county magistrate has complied with this order, but in the event of a famine, no delay is allowed. Therefore, the county magistrate is ordered to comply with the previous order and handle the matter seriously, without treating it as a mere formality, lest it cause inconvenience, and report the handling situation at any time. This order!

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Studies Year-End Closing Issues 108

The use of the Gregorian calendar for year-end closing by businesses has been officially mandated by the National Government. However, recent opinions expressed by various trade associations indicate that, due to the agricultural nature of our country, a large-scale year-end closing is feared to cause various obstacles. It is proposed to petition for approval to postpone the implementation in accordance with business practices. It is reported that the Municipal Chamber of Commerce considers this matter to be of great importance and has submitted it to the fifth regular meeting of the Executive Committee of the Chamber on the 17th of this month to discuss this issue. It was resolved that a committee should be organized to conduct a detailed study before submitting it to the Executive Committee for discussion. Zhu Yinjiang, Luo Qinghua, Lu Wenshao, Wang Yansong, and Xu Jiqing were publicly elected as members and will begin the study immediately.

Year-End Closing on the Gregorian Calendar 109

Rice Milling Industry Also Requests Postponement

The Shanghai Rice Milling Trade Association submitted a document to the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau yesterday, stating:

Petition for Postponement of Year-End Closing for the Nineteenth Year, Requesting Approval to Alleviate Business Difficulties. Our association has twice followed the Gregorian calendar for year-end closing at the fifth and ninth months, and the difficulties encountered are the same as those reported by the bean and rice merchants' association. This has been observed for a long time and need not be repeated. We believe that the unification of the national calendar is one thing, and the year-end closing of businesses is another. We must not think that requesting a postponement of the year-end closing implies a desire to abandon the Gregorian calendar, nor can we consider alleviating business difficulties to be a superstitious practice. Although the government's policy implementation should not be delayed by long-standing difficulties, reforming customs requires careful consideration of public sentiment to gradually move towards the right track. The accounts from the previous fifth and ninth months have not yet been fully settled. If a postponement is not granted, it will inevitably lead to hardship for businesses and farmers. Is the government's reform of the Gregorian calendar specifically intended to cause hardship for businesses and farmers? We believe that postponing the year-end closing would hinder the promotion of the Gregorian calendar. After careful deliberation, we believe that reforming the Gregorian calendar and the year-end closing of businesses are two separate matters. Therefore, we specifically submit this document to support the suggestion of the bean and rice merchants' association to request a postponement of the year-end closing. We sincerely hope that the Bureau will consider the difficulties of businesses and grant the request. We eagerly await your response and respectfully submit this to the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau.

Record of the Silk Factory Trade Association General Meeting 116

Abolishing Cocoon Exchanges...Reducing Taxes...Improving Inspection The Shanghai Silk Factory Trade Association convened a general meeting of all silk factories in Shanghai at 3 p.m. on the 19th. Executive Committee members Zhu Jingan, Huang Jinfan, Zhang Peishen, and others, as well as more than 130 representatives from all factories, attended. Shen Huachen chaired the meeting and, after performing the rituals, first submitted the outline of the resolution of the Special Committee for the Relief of the Silk Industry, which requested the government to issue 10 million yuan in public bonds for the silk industry in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai to cover losses and provide guarantees, to the attendees for a vote. It was unanimously passed. Regarding the method of distributing the bond amount, it was resolved that it should be directly distributed to each factory. Subsequently, the representatives resolved three major issues: (1) The proposal to abolish cocoon exchanges in various provinces. The attendees noted that since the implementation of opening up cocoon exchanges, the number of newly added cocoon exchanges in various provinces has been increasing almost daily. However, the production of silkworm cocoons is limited. With more exchanges and less goods, they inevitably engage in price competition, leading to high cocoon prices. Farmers, seeing the high cocoon prices, increase the number of silkworm eggs they raise. The supply of mulberry leaves is insufficient, and the silkworms are fed before they have enough leaves, resulting in thin and inferior cocoons that are not suitable for silk reeling. The raw materials for silk factories are thus becoming increasingly scarce. It is urgent to restrict the establishment of cocoon exchanges to avoid price competition and reduce the cost of cocoons. At the same time, a survey should be conducted on the production of mulberry leaves in various silkworm-producing areas to determine the appropriate number of silkworm eggs to raise, in order to ensure the quality of cocoons. It was resolved to petition the government to separately abolish them. (2) The proposal to reduce the burden on the industry. The attendees noted that silk, tea, and other items from our country are the largest exports in trade. The government should provide encouragement to promote the development of Chinese silk, which is of utmost importance. The price of Chinese silk trade usually fluctuates with the market price abroad, and the rise and fall of foreign firms' prices are difficult to predict. The right to bargain is in the hands of foreign merchants. It is urgent to petition the government to exempt cocoon taxes and export silk taxes to reduce the burden and lower costs, in order to compete for survival. It was resolved to urge the government to effectively reduce and exempt taxes to maintain the silk industry. (3) The proposal for public weighing and inspection of factory silk. The chairman reported that Mr. Wang Xiaolai of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce had previously invited both parties to talk, and the Bureau had acknowledged that the public weighing and inspection has value for research and improvement in the future. The attendees believed that if the public weighing and inspection is to continue in the future, the improvement plan must be clearly announced first to convince people. It is not possible to ignore it and muddle through. It was resolved to urge Mr. Wang Xiaolai to press the Commodity Inspection Bureau to provide a concrete response. The meeting adjourned after the discussion at 9:30 p.m.

Silk Inspection Office Investigates the Recent Situation of Silk Factories 117

The sales of raw silk are most dependent on the United States. Recently, credit has become unusually tight in the United States, causing silk sales to stagnate. Japanese and Italian silk have been greatly affected, and Chinese silk is unlikely to escape this exception. Many silk factories in Shanghai have suspended operations due to this impact. Director Miao of the Raw Silk Inspection Office of the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau is very concerned about this matter. He recently sent staff from the office to six districts, including Hongkou, Zhabei, South Bund, North Bund, West Shanghai, and Tientongan, to conduct a thorough investigation of the recent situation of various silk factories. The current statistics show that out of 106 silk factories in Shanghai, 60 have suspended operations, 43 have not suspended operations, and 3 are operating intermittently. The period of suspension for the factories that have suspended operations is mostly from the end of August to the beginning of September.

Another Large Batch of Chinese Laborers Sent Back by Japanese Authorities 118

Due to the contraction of various factories and fields in Japan this year, many Chinese laborers in Japan have been laid off and cannot survive. As a result, many batches have been sent back to China by the Japanese authorities. Recently, a group of laid-off Chinese from Ishijima-cho, Omori-cho, and Mikawashima in Tokyo Prefecture were sent back to Shanghai by the Tokyo Metropolitan Police Department with the consent of our country's embassy in Japan because they had no means of livelihood. The group included 22 workers: Zhou Qinlin, Pan Tingxi, Pan Ali, Huang Richang, Zhou Youfu, Mei Aliang, Wu Zhenyou, Huang Yinbiao, Wu Yanzhou, Wu Yanxi, Li Deji, and others. There were also 10 laborers: Lin Shangzhou, Zhou Xiannan, Wang Shixia, Xia Zuodong, Jiang Yanxing, Zhu Chengmei, Liu Yinmei, Chen Yazuo, and others. They were all escorted to Shanghai on the Japanese ship Tsukuba Maru. The Japanese Embassy had telegraphed the Shanghai Public Security Bureau in advance, requesting that personnel be sent to assist with disembarkation. Therefore, the Public Security Bureau sent personnel to the dock to assist when the Tsukuba Maru entered the port. Most of the repatriated Chinese laborers were from Qingtian County, Zhejiang Province. They were all in a miserable state upon their return. It is now planned to send these laborers back to their original homes in Eastern Zhejiang.

For example, the Machinery Department used to have only one person, Muller, but now a deputy, Moohnn, has been added, and recently another person has been added, whose name is unknown. As for the Russian people, they were brought in by the manager on the pretext of laziness. The former manager, who served for decades, never had any laziness in the factory. The current manager rejects the requests of Chinese workers, but after three months of work for British people in the factory, they are given a raise, and after three years of service, they are given six months of vacation to return home. In addition, they also have one month of vacation each year. Chinese workers do not receive such preferential treatment. Although Chinese workers work eight hours, they are often mistreated by British and Russian people. The former lower-level British person, Dounalay, even fired more than ten old Chinese workers who had been in the factory for more than ten years. Later, he was fired recently because he got into a dispute with a fellow British person while drunk. Others, such as the current MeMahen and Gohons, are also fierce and treat Chinese workers as enemies. These people not only increase expenses but also easily create resentment. In fact, they should not be hired. Under the former manager, there was also Shen Anfu, who had a monthly salary of more than eighty yuan. Since Shen's death, there has been no foreman with a salary of more than seventy yuan, except for a copper craftsman foreman. Also, the number of people in the chemical laboratory has increased from one to four. All of these issues need to be changed urgently. If the manager says that the three shifts of British people should not be completely removed, then Chinese people can be used to replace them. As for the Russian people and the three British deputies, they must be completely removed. If ten percent of the savings are given to the Chinese as foremen and long-term workers, then labor unrest will never occur again. Not only will the water price not need to be increased, but it can also be greatly reduced. Wouldn't that be killing multiple birds with one stone? We are now publishing the original letter and requesting that the Shanghai Real Estate Association inform the citizens so that all residents of the city can have a deep understanding and sympathy. They will inevitably rise up to make this firm demand. Even for future price increases, we can use this as a basis for negotiations. We are writing to you for your information and reference." This letter is addressed to the Shanghai Real Estate Association.

However, the new tax pledge regulations have been submitted by the Tea Industry Association to be handled in accordance with the guarantee regulations, but approval has not yet been received. As for tea that is transferred to foreign countries, taxes should be paid first, and then the export customs will refund the taxes upon export. According to a telegram from Hankou received by the company yesterday, the damaged small ship was stranded on a shallow sandbar on the riverbank at the time. The ship did not sink, so all passengers and crew members were rescued and transported to Hankou by the Xianghe ship. They have now arrived safely. The extent of the damage to the ship is still under investigation.

City Government Issues Regulations for Municipal Citizen Oath Registration 124

According to Articles 6, 7, and 85 of the Municipal Organization Law regarding municipal citizen oath registration, a necessary procedure for citizens to obtain municipal citizenship, the Ministry of Interior recently drafted "Regulations for Municipal Citizen Oath Registration" based on the aforementioned articles of the law. These regulations were submitted to and approved by the Executive Yuan for promulgation and are to be universally followed. The municipal government of this port received a dispatch from the Ministry of Interior yesterday transmitting the aforementioned regulations. It immediately ordered all bureaus and district councils to comply. The articles of the regulations are recorded as follows: (Article 1) These regulations are formulated in accordance with the procedures stipulated in Articles 6, 7, and 85 of the Municipal Organization Law. (Article 2) Anyone who possesses the qualifications stipulated in Article 6, Paragraph 1 of the Municipal Organization Law, upon taking an oath and registering, becomes a municipal citizen. (Article 3) Oaths are divided into the following two types: (1) Regular oaths: The ward office investigates qualifications two months before the annual ward residents' meeting and convenes the oath-taking ceremony. (2) Temporary oaths: People may request the ward office to investigate their qualifications at any time and convene an oath-taking ceremony. For the aforementioned temporary oaths, the ward office may choose a date depending on the number of people, but if people need to take the oath quickly due to necessary circumstances, they should request it according to schedule. (Article 4) The oath-taking ceremony is held at the ward office, with the ward head as the chairman. When the ward office has not been established, the aforementioned oath-taking ceremony should be held at the district office, and the chairman is the district head or a designated district assistant. (Article 5) The oath should be made in duplicate (Form 1). First, people go to the ward office to register for verification and personally sign both copies of the oath. The ward office then issues one copy of the oath to be returned at the time of the regular oath-taking ceremony as proof of oath. People who cannot sign may handle it according to Article 2, Paragraph 2 or Paragraph 3 of the General Principles of the Civil Law. (Article 6) During the oath-taking ceremony, personnel from the district office are dispatched to supervise. The procedure is as follows: (1) Everyone stands at attention. (2) Sing the Party anthem. (3) Bow three times to the national flag, the Party flag, and the portrait of the late Premier. (4) The chairman respectfully reads the late Premier's will. (5) People raise their right hands, state their names, and read the oath. (6) Chairman's speech. (7) Supervising official's speech. (8) Ceremony concludes. People who cannot read the oath may have the chairman lead the reading. (Article 7) After the people have taken the oath, the ward office should establish a citizen roster (Form 2) to register them as municipal citizens. When the ward office has not been established, the aforementioned registration is handled by the district office. (Article 8) The ward office should create two copies of the citizen roster, submitting one copy to the district office and the other copy, along with the oaths, to the district office for submission to the municipal government for record-keeping. When the ward office has not been established, the aforementioned citizen roster is created in duplicate by the district office, with one copy submitted to the municipal government for record-keeping along with the oaths. The remaining copy is transferred to the ward office for verification when it is established. The oaths and citizen rosters for temporary oaths under Article 3 of these regulations are handled according to the aforementioned two procedures. (Article 9) After registering municipal citizens, if the ward office discovers that they have any of the circumstances listed in Article 6, Paragraph 2 of the Municipal Organization Law, it may, in accordance with the law, petition the district office to request the municipal government to revoke their citizenship, remove their registration, and announce it publicly. (Article 10) After municipal citizens are registered, regardless of which ward they move to within the municipality, they should report to the ward office for notification to the ward office of their new residence (Form 3) for transfer of registration (Form 4). The aforementioned transfer registration involves citizenship rights. (Article 11) When a municipal citizen dies, the ward office should cancel their registration. (Article 12) The ward office should report changes in the circumstances of municipal citizens to the municipal government through the district office on a monthly basis for record-keeping. (Article 13) These regulations may be handled by each municipal government within the scope stipulated in Articles 6, 7, and 85 of the Municipal Organization Law, taking into account local conditions. (Article 14) These regulations shall come into effect on the date of promulgation.

Dispatching Personnel to Supervise the Reorganization of Mass Organizations 125

▲Zhang Renjie dispatched by Shanghai to provide guidance

Sixth District, Nineteenth Branch Declares 法(french) Sailors' Rampage 128

According to the National News Agency, the Nineteenth Branch of the Sixth District of this city issued a declaration against the unreasonable rampage of French sailors, which resulted in the tragic death of boatman Xin Dingchang. "To the newspaper offices and public organizations across the country: Unfortunately, our country has been plagued by internal strife in recent years. Imperialists, relying on unequal treaties as their talisman, run rampant everywhere in our country, killing people like flies. These imperialists have no remorse and are taking advantage of our central government's involvement in the Northwest. Their arrogance is intensifying. For example, on the evening of the 16th of this month, at 7 p.m., Xin Dingchang, a Ningbo native, was rowing sampan number 130, which was moored at the jetty on Weituoma Road, Yangshupu, and then moored between the tenth and twenty-third buoys of the customs there. Two sailors from the French (Chenonceaux) merchant ship hailed Xin's sampan to ferry them to the ship. After the two sailors boarded the ship, they did not pay, so they waited for an hour. Then they saw them board another ship to go ashore. Xin asked them for the fare. Unexpectedly, the sailors had no sense and became extremely impatient. Without any explanation, they dragged Xin, punching and kicking him. Xin was caught off guard and was suddenly knocked into the river, his body sinking to the bottom, resulting in his tragic death. When the sailors saw that they had caused the disaster, they boarded another ship and left, treating the lives of our people as less than chickens and dogs. If our people do not rise up quickly to seek justice, our nation will have no future. The sailors should have tried to rescue Xin when they saw him fall into the river, but they allowed him to drown, which is extremely inhumane. We deeply hope that compatriots across the country will rise up together and pledge to be the diplomatic backup. It is not just for the death of Xin alone, but for the great shame and humiliation of our nation. All the people in this branch are willing to use our utmost determination to achieve the goal of punishing the perpetrators, providing compensation, and issuing an apology. This is our declaration."

Qingyun Lane Tenants' Association States the Forced Experience 130

The Qingyun Lane Tenants' Association yesterday copied and published the letter from the lawyer Gao Yi, representing the New Sassoon Company, in response to the Shanghai Special District Citizens' Federation. It also provided an explanation of the circumstances in which the landlord forced the demolition of the houses, awaiting public judgment. The details are recorded separately as follows: (Lawyer Gao Yi's reply to the Citizens' Federation) "Dear Sirs, I have just received your letter from my client, the New Sassoon Company, regarding the property in Qingyun Lane, and I am writing on its behalf to reply. Upon investigation, the people currently living in the houses in Qingyun Lane are no longer considered tenants but are considered trespassers who are illegally occupying the property. My client has the right to dispose of its property as it sees fit. The words stated in Section 2 of your letter are difficult for my client to acknowledge. However, my client is obviously not responsible for any losses caused by the illegal resistance of the trespassers. As for the final section of your letter, if the trespassers claim to have suffered injustice, they can take any legal steps they wish to deal with it. Since they have not taken legal steps, my client assumes that the trespassers have not suffered any injustice. I am writing to inform you accordingly and hope that you will take note of it." (Statement by the Tenants' Association) "The circumstances of the demolition: On June 26 of this year, the tenants of Qingyun Lane received a notice from the company stating that the houses would be renovated and demanding that all tenants completely move out and return the houses by the end of August. The tenants of our lane then sent representatives to visit the manager of the company and the rental buyer Xing Dingyong, recounting the difficulties the tenants had in moving and voluntarily offering to increase the rent to request that they withdraw the order. At the same time, they requested various organizations to act as mediators. After they left, the company did not express whether it would accept the request or send a final eviction notice. Unexpectedly, on September 10, the tragedy of white Russian thugs injuring people and looting property occurred. Upon investigation, the company did not have a demolition permit or build fences, yet it dared to commit violence in broad daylight. Its intention was nothing more than to expose the hideous face of imperialists who destroy weak nations and despise our country, thinking that even if they trample on China, it can do nothing about it. Furthermore, claiming that the tenants are illegally occupying the property, they can sue in court and request deportation. Now they are using such illegal tactics that disregard international friendship, and Sima Zhao's intentions are revealed. Who would believe that they do not despise our country? The suffering of those personally affected is not worth mentioning, but what about the dignity of our country? Therefore, after careful consideration, both feelings of resentment and pain cannot be mixed up with the dispute between the landlord and the tenants. Therefore, we all have the determination to fight to the death to achieve the goal of seeking redress. In addition to submitting a petition, we have also lodged a serious protest with the authorities against the other party, demanding that they formally apologize to our government and compensate for the losses. We have also announced the circumstances of the victimization and refuted their letter, hoping that people from all walks of life across the country will make a fair judgment. Qingyun Lane Tenants' Association, October 19, 1920."

The Number of Japanese Residents Decreases 134

There are currently 25,300+ People

Compared to the Last Survey, the Number Decreased by 1,000

According to the announcement made yesterday by the Japanese Consulate General in Shanghai, the total number of Japanese residents in Shanghai surveyed by order of the government has been completed. The actual number of Japanese residents in Shanghai is 25,376. Among them, the textile industry has the largest number of people, with 4,922 people. Compared with the last survey, the number has decreased by more than 1,000. The reason for this is that the recession in Japan has led to most companies and institutions laying off employees and returning to their home country, which has greatly reduced the number of people. Yesterday, the Japanese government officially notified of the verification.

Jisheng Society Races to Make Cotton Clothes for Disaster Areas 135

Hoping All Sectors Will Help Revitalize the Manufacturing of Clothing and Floss

The China Jisheng Society in this port believes that it is now late autumn and the severe winter is approaching. The provinces that have been most severely affected by disasters, such as Henan, Shaanxi, Liaoning, and Ningxia, are lacking food in the winter and have no clothes. The wilderness is full of cries of hunger and cold. The society is now rushing to make cotton clothes to be transported for emergency relief. If people from all walks of life have donations and cotton clothes to help revitalize the disaster relief efforts, they are asked to send them to the society as soon as possible so that they can be transported in batches for relief. Clothing floss is always warmer when it is newly made. The severe cold in the north makes old cotton useless. Please pay attention to this.

The Loud Call of the Overseas Chinese Federation

Wife Escapes, Lawsuit Involved 140

Over Fifty Against Twenty-Four

Elder Brother Unjustly Beaten

Women's Association Difficult to Mediate

Guangdong native Jin Dekang, age fifty-four, resides at No. 18, Songbaili, Qiujiang Road, Zhabei. He has been working as a scribe at the Xinshichang Foreign Firm on Avenue Joffre in the French Concession for over thirty years. His wife passed away, leaving behind children without care. Therefore, in 1928, he went to a certain hall and obtained a Suzhou woman, Wang Guizhen, as his second wife. The woman is currently twenty-four years old and extremely beautiful. Since entering the household, seeing that Jin was old, although his family wealth was abundant, their marital relationship was ultimately unhappy, leading to frequent conflicts. In December of last year, Guizhen secretly fled her husband. After losing his wife, Jin searched everywhere without any news. Subsequently, his brother, Mr. Jin, who resembled Dekang, one day happened to pass through the French Concession when he was suddenly surrounded by many hooligans. Without distinguishing right from wrong, they brutally assaulted him. Mr. Jin was outnumbered and seriously injured. He immediately returned and told his younger brother Dekang. While they were still puzzled, the next day they suddenly received an anonymous letter, the main point of which was that the beating that day was originally intended for your brother, but they mistakenly identified you, causing you injury. They expressed much apology. Soon after, Dekang also received a phone call at the same time. Listening closely to the accent, it seemed to be from Guizhen, saying, "I am in Shanghai, you don't need to search for me. If you continue to search," then the voice suddenly changed to a man's voice, loudly continuing, "If you continue to search, I will deal with you with a gun. Be careful," and so on. At this point, Dekang finally realized that his brother's assault was actually caused by him. Recalling Guizhen's cruelty, he couldn't help but feel great anger and went to the court to file a lawsuit. Soon, he received a judgment to wait until the defendant was found for further investigation. Unexpectedly, Dekang recently received a notice from the Women's Association stating that Wang Guizhen was currently at the association, requesting assistance in breaking off relations with him. Jin immediately went to the association, intending to reconcile with both parties, but without success. Until yesterday afternoon around 4:00 PM, Jin went again for negotiations without reaching an agreement. He then called upon Guo Yuling, the guard police officer from the Fifth Post, to bring Wang Guizhen and others to the Third Sub-District of the First District, where the director conducted a preliminary hearing. Jin Dekang explained the situation, and Wang Guizhen stated in her confession that her biological parents' surnames were unknown, but she was raised from a young age by an elderly woman surnamed Wang in Suzhou. Later, the elderly woman, seeing that her appearance was quite good, intended to sell her to a brothel. Hearing this, she refused and threw herself into a hall for care. Three years ago, Jin Dekang, accompanied by another young man, came and claimed that they wanted to take her to England to study, so she was taken out. Later, she realized she had been deceived and had no choice but to escape and seek help from the Women's Association, requesting assistance. The negotiations still had no results, etc. The director ordered that a document be prepared and sent to the Shanghai District Court for interrogation.

Elementary School Teacher Encounters Jiangbei Bandit Leader on the Road 141

Reports to the Police and Intercepts Him

Xing Xiumin, a teacher at the Jianghuai Shanghai Elementary School on Taiyang Temple Road in Zhabei, was wandering along the railway tracks there yesterday afternoon after finishing work when he caught sight of a person walking slowly ahead of him, appearing to be considering something. He looked closer and was shocked to see that the person's appearance closely resembled Lu Jinbao, a well-known bandit from Jiangbei. He immediately reported to the head of the Taiyang Temple Police Station in the Fourth District, who rushed to arrest him and transferred him to headquarters. According to Xing's account, Lu Jinbao was a bandit leader in Funing, Yancheng, and other places in Jiangbei, and had committed several cases of murder and kidnapping. The local authorities had issued a strict arrest warrant. Today, he unexpectedly encountered him on the road. At first, he looked at him repeatedly to confirm, but the person was guilty and tried to hire a car to escape, so he reported it to the police for arrest, etc. In his interrogation, the man denied being Lu Jinbao, claiming his name was Li Zhuoru, a native of Yancheng, who had always been a law-abiding merchant. He vehemently denied the accusations. Headquarters examined the confession and, considering the seriousness of the case, ordered him to be detained for further investigation.

Japanese Man Hangs Himself 142

Hangs Himself on a Willow Branch

Branch Breaks and He Falls into the Pond

Yesterday afternoon at around 2:10 PM, south of Caojiadu in western Shanghai, north of Avenue Henri Brenier, in the Sujiakou area behind Zhaofeng Garden, next to the weedy pond in front of the Wusheng Temple, a Japanese man wearing a blue woolen suit was suddenly discovered. He had hanged himself from a willow tree with a leather belt and had already fallen into the pond. The local villagers spotted him and reported it to the Sixth District Police Station. The district chief, Director Ren, personally inspected the scene and ordered the local Baojia to report to the District Court for an autopsy. Around 4:00 PM in the afternoon, Prosecutor Guo arrived with the coroner to conduct the autopsy. First, the body was fished out and placed on the bank. It was found that the Japanese man was about twenty-seven or eight years old and had indeed hanged himself from a tree branch with a leather belt, which broke due to its tenderness, causing the body to fall into the pond. His entire body was drenched with water. It was heard that the Japanese man was a training doctor on a certain Japanese warship, twenty-eight years old. He had taken this world-weary action due to some domestic stimulation. The officers of the warship found out and immediately rushed there with the detectives from the Jing'an Temple West Police Station, and then immediately took measures to collect the body and prepare the coffin, etc.

Chen Zili's Death Telegraph 146

A Cantonese merchant in this port received a telegram from Guangdong stating that Mr. Chen Zili of Dongguan, courtesy name Botao, was a former Qing Dynasty Tanhua (third-ranking scholar in the imperial examination) who served as the chief examiner in Yunnan, Guizhou, and Shandong, and as the Jiangning Commissioner of Education. Jinan University was founded by his hand. He then requested to retire to care for his elderly mother. Xiang Cheng (Yuan Shikai) repeatedly urged him to come out of the mountains as the Guangdong Governor, but he declined with strong words. He spent his days wandering in Kowloon City, dedicating himself to writing. He authored works such as "Commentary on the Classic of Filial Piety," "Biographies of the Five Loyalists of Dongguan," "Record of Ming Dynasty Loyalists of Dongguan," and "Dongguan County Chronicle," which were published. He passed away in Kowloon on October 11 at the age of seventy-six.

Barge Capsizes in the Wind 147

Crew Members Fall into the Water, All Rescued

Yesterday, the sea breeze at Songkou was very strong. At around 8:00 AM, a barge carrying goods between Shanghai and Yuepu was sailing through the Pu River near Zhanghuabang when a sudden gust of wind caused the barge to lose control and suddenly capsize. All the crew members fell into the water. Fortunately, the patrol boat of the Wusongkou Lifesaving Bureau bravely came forward to rescue them and completely rescued the crew members Jiang Ahu, Gu Yaoqi, and others, preventing them from drowning. They also towed the capsized barge to a shallow beach on the riverbank. They reported the situation to the Lifesaving Bureau. Director He Xiaohong of the Bureau questioned the rescued crew members and ordered them to go to the beach and take back and repair the overturned boat.

Wang Chongwen Passed Away the Day Before Yesterday 148

Former Navy Commander Wang Chongwen came to Shanghai from Fujian some time ago to recuperate. On the 19th of this month, he suddenly suffered a stroke at the Baolong Hospital. Despite the efforts of famous Chinese and foreign doctors, it was ineffective, and he passed away at noon that day. It is heard that his family has scheduled the coffin to be sealed at the International Funeral Home at 5:00 PM today (the 21st).

End Table and Side Table Have False Bottoms Hiding Cigarettes 149

Shanghai South Station of the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway, yesterday morning at 7:15 AM, the first-class early passenger train was about to depart, and preparations were being made for the second-class fourth train. Suddenly, a man about forty years old, wearing a black gown and a copper-basin felt hat, with a follower about thirty years old, wearing short clothes and resembling a rickshaw puller, hired a rickshaw carrying an end table (drawing table) and two side tables, wrapped with bamboo strips. After the passenger arrived at the station, he did not purchase a passenger ticket but first moved the end table and side tables to the luggage room to make a ticket. The baggage clerk said that according to the regulations, a passenger ticket was required to make an account. While they were handing over, Wang Zheng, the director of the inspection department dispatched to the station by the Songhu Garrison Command, and the investigating military police, seeing that the end table and side tables looked suspicious, stepped forward to dismantle them. Upon inspection, the end table and side tables were indeed made with false bottoms, hiding a large number of cigarettes, totaling twelve large packages and more than eighty small packages, more than one hundred packages in total, worth about two thousand yuan. The people and goods were detained and reported to the command for handling.

Detestable Female Con Artist 150

Yesterday afternoon, Zhang Yuhua, who claimed to be a female teacher at the Xiafei Road Art School, went to the home of Li Zhongwen, a translator at the Guomin Newspaper on Shanhai Pass Road, seeking help. Li met with her and, not recognizing her, asked her purpose. She claimed that her elder brother was a classmate of yours at the Dongwu Law School, and now, because her eldest child had died prematurely and her younger child was ill, she wanted to send them to the hospital for treatment. Her husband was far away in another port and lacked funds, so she begged to borrow five yuan temporarily, which she would return as soon as she received her salary. Li listened and, seeing that her clothes were neat and her speech elegant, did not think she was a con artist, so he replied that there were many con artists outside now. If you are in urgent need, you can leave an address, and I will send it to you. Unexpectedly, the woman said that she needed to buy things now. If it was inconvenient, could you temporarily give me two yuan? Li thought the amount was small, so he gave it to her, and told her that this was not because of a classmate's face, but because you are a woman, so I am helping you. Later, Li heard that this woman had gone to Yang Qianli's house seeking help, also seeking assistance in the same way. She was scolded by Yang's eldest son, and the woman left in shame.

Mixing in Counterfeit Fifty-Cent Bills 151

Falsely Claiming to Use Money to Redeem Tickets

Bringing Back to the Hometown for Use

The day before yesterday morning around 10:00 AM, Liu Quande, a native of Haimen, mixed in a counterfeit fifty-cent bill at Xu Liqi's cigarette and paper shop at No. 89 Yalü Road, which was detected by Xu. He questioned him, and they quarreled with each other. An Huabu No. 1906 happened to pass by, and after learning the situation, arrested Liu and searched his body, finding 167 similar counterfeit fifty-cent bills and 61 pawn tickets, which were all taken to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Third Criminal Court of the Special Zone. The police lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, stated the case, saying that the defendant had confessed at the police station that the counterfeit bills were purchased from someone surnamed Mou on Baoshan Road in the Chinese territory. He then handed over the two counterfeit bills to the Public Security Bureau for investigation of the seller. Xu Liqi also submitted a case report, proving the situation at the time. Interrogated the defendant, who confessed that he came to Shanghai from his hometown only two days ago. Previously, his fellow villager Shi Zi'an was kidnapped by bandits and extorted two thousand yuan for a ransom. He was entrusted by his friend to purchase the above-mentioned counterfeit bills, totaling ten yuan, from someone surnamed Mou on Baoshan Road to bring back to his hometown to pay to the bandits on behalf of Shi. Yesterday, while passing by the plaintiff's shop, he intended to try using the counterfeit bill but was arrested. He asked for judgment. The police lawyer Zhang also stated that a large number of pawn tickets were found from the defendant in the police station. Asked about the inside story, he claimed that he had been unemployed in Shanghai for a year, so he gradually pawned his clothes to make a living. The defendant's confession did not match, and the claim that he wanted to bring the counterfeit bills back to his hometown to pay the bandits was even more nonsense. Judge Feng Shide examined the confession and, after designating lawyer Jiang Baoli as the defendant's pro bono defense, ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody pending sentencing.

Teenager Commits Suicide by Poisoning in Hotel 152

Suicide Note Says Life is Tasteless

Sent to Hospital for Treatment, Died Ineffective

Last Saturday evening around 6:30 PM, a teenager in a Western suit entered the Yadong Hotel on Wuma Road. The tea servant No. 30 led him to room 437. The registration book only stated Lin Lang from Fujian, age twenty-eight, academic, came to Shanghai from Zhenru, and told the tea servant that tomorrow was Sunday, so he could sleep later and did not need to be called, etc. The tea servant readily agreed and left. Yesterday noon after 12:00 PM, the tea servant saw that he had not yet gotten up. Due to the hotel regulations, he had to knock on the door and call. After several minutes, there was no response, so he tried to pry open the door. He saw that Lin was unconscious and his breathing was weak. A note was left on the table, the content of which was roughly that the world was vast and tasteless, so it was better to go to the underworld early to end this life, etc. He immediately hired a car and sent him to Renji Hospital for treatment. Because medical treatment was ineffective, he died at around 8:00 AM yesterday morning.

Escaped Wife Dragged Out from Under the Bed 154

Zhang Yuhong, a native of Yancheng, worked in Xinghua and married a woman surnamed Qiu as his wife. The woman was twenty-seven years old this year. During the Qingming Festival this year, the woman suddenly disappeared without a trace in Xinghua. After losing his wife, Zhang investigated from spring to summer, and from summer to autumn, until now, as winter was approaching, he learned that the woman had eloped with Lü Changming and was hiding at No. 2, Junli, Gujiating, Haichao Temple in the South City. Yesterday morning, he filed a complaint at the Third Sub-District of the First District, who dispatched police to assist in arresting Lü. However, after searching everywhere, the woman was nowhere to be found. Later, because he saw that the behavior inside No. 3 next door was suspicious, he went to search again. Unexpectedly, the woman was hiding under the bed, cowering and afraid to make a sound. They immediately dragged her out and escorted them to the station, and then transferred them to the District Court for interrogation.

Gu Jiemin's Free Concubine's Despotic Control 155

Breaks off Family Relations, Gives Two Thousand Yuan

Not Allowed to Use Gu's Name, etc.

Gu Jiemin, a gold merchant, is twenty-six years old, from Pinghu, Zhejiang, and does business in Shanghai. In the spring of 1927, he was playing with friends in the brothels and became acquainted with the prostitute Pei Qiaoxian, who is now nineteen years old, from Suzhou. Jiemin and Qiaoxian fell in love at first sight, reported their affection, and became extraordinarily loving after several months. In December of that year, they discussed the silver to redeem her with the madam, paid it, and took her as a concubine, bringing her back to the house, renaming her Gu Pei Qian, courtesy name Suman. The following year (1928), he sent Qiaoxian to study at the Wang's Women's School in this port, where she stayed, only returning home on Sundays. For three years, Qiaoxian was absorbed in social life and liked to be fashionable, and her clothes and jewelry were unusually gorgeous. Subsequently, because Jiemin had parents in the hall, who were old-fashioned, they repeatedly blamed her when they saw this situation. Qiaoxian did not abide by etiquette, and Qiaoxian believed that the current situation was free and equal, and she would not accept despotic control, so disputes arose at this time. A few days ago, a dispute occurred, and Qiaoxian took two boxes of clothes and left, leaving them at her sister's house, and hired a lawyer to negotiate with Jiemin, requesting to break off family relations. It is heard that the negotiations were successful, and the conditions for breaking off family relations included giving her two thousand yuan in cash for Qiaoxian's living expenses, and handing over all clothes and jewelry to Qiaoxian to collect. Lawyer Chen Ying was hired to certify the contract, but after the contract was broken, she was not allowed to use names such as Gu Pei Qian and Su Man.

Young Girl Abused, Seriously Injured, and Died 156

Cao Qiu is Detained by the Police Station

Chen Meibao, the thirteen-year-old niece of Chen Lin, a woman from Ningbo living at No. 4, Zhufuli, Qiujiang Road, Shanghai North, lost her father early. Her mother came to Shanghai last year due to illness and was treated at Renji Hospital. Later, through the recommendation of Zhang Li, a female missionary of the Jesus Church, Meibao was recommended to learn Western socks at the home of Cao Qiu, an elderly woman from Pudong, at No. 1, Puqingli, Ma Lang Road, French Concession. Unexpectedly, Qiu was fierce, and after Meibao entered her house, it was like entering the gate of hell. If she slightly disobeyed, she would be beaten with rods. Neighbors often heard tragic cries that were unbearable. Unexpectedly, on the 13th of this month, Qiu beat Meibao again, causing injury to her waist. She was sent to Renji Hospital for treatment. After the doctor found internal injuries, he operated. However, the injury was serious, and the treatment was ineffective. She died at twelve o'clock that night. The woman did not report to the police station. Just as she was about to buy a coffin for burial, the matter was learned by neighbors, who were very indignant and reported to the police station. Detectives brought Qiu in for questioning. She admitted to beating. The police chief ordered her to be detained and ordered detectives to carry Meibao's body to the Tongren Fuyuantang autopsy station, and reported to Judge Zhu Cheng of the French Public Concession Court to conduct an autopsy, ordering the police station to select a Western doctor for examination. Because the deceased's family was poor, the church member Zhang Qilin prepared a coffin for burial on their behalf, pending verification. Yesterday, the police station sent Qiu to the French Public Concession Court for investigation. First, the police chief reported that the Western doctor had examined Meibao's body and found bruises all over her body, and that the intestines in her abdomen were pierced, proving that the woman had been beaten too much by the defendant before her death. The examination report was submitted for inspection. Witnesses Zhu Jingqing and Wang Shuofu testified that they had heard beating sounds and Meibao's crying sounds from Qiu's room when they lived with Qiu, and that they reported it to the police station out of indignation. Interrogated Cao Qiu, who confessed that Meibao was recommended by Zhang Li to learn to weave Western socks. Because she was stupid, Cao Yuzhen, the woman's daughter, slightly blamed her. The rest of her confession was evasive. The Chinese and Western officials ordered Qiu to be remanded in custody pending further investigation.

Chicken Vendor Goes Missing Due to Nervous Breakdown 158

Where is Zhang Ronggui from Qingjiang?

Zhang Ronggui, a native of Qingjiang, age fifty-eight, was a chicken vendor. Zhang came to Shanghai from his hometown on the 14th of this month to sell chickens. After selling the goods, he stayed at the Deyuan Chicken Shop in Laotaiping Lane, Shiliupu. He suddenly suffered a nervous breakdown, crying and laughing erratically all day long, due to some unknown stimulus. On the 18th, his companion intended to send him back to his hometown, but Zhang ran wildly midway, shouting for help. The police on duty heard it and rushed over and took Zhang to the First District Headquarters. After questioning, they ordered him to be released on bail, ordering him to be properly guarded. Unexpectedly, Zhang suddenly disappeared the day before yesterday morning. His companions searched everywhere without finding him. Hiding Grudges and Randomly Pouring Caustic Soda 159

Xu Liansheng and Others Separately Imprisoned

Shen Zhu, a woman from Shaoxing residing at No. 2018, Xinzha Road, and her eighteen-year-old daughter Shen Azhen, were attacked by Azhen's lover Zhu Zhongrong, together with Xu Liansheng, Wang Weixiang, Zhang Huangguang, Li Zigang, Chen Ruilin, Yang Liubao, etc., using硝水 at their home on the afternoon of the 5th of this month, splashing it all over Azhen's face, causing serious injuries, and Shen Zhu's face was also affected. The case was reported to the Xinzha Police Station, who dispatched detectives Zhang Ankang to arrest Xu and the other six people, while Zhu Zhongrong was on the run. They were sent to the Special Zone Court for interrogation and imprisonment, as reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, the date for the continued interrogation arrived. The police lawyer Wang Yaotang stated that the main culprit in this case, Zhu Zhongrong, had still not been apprehended, and the injured Shen Azhen had not yet recovered and was still in the hospital. However, according to the previous order, the defendants were sent to the hospital to examine whether they had any caustic soda scars on their bodies. The police have now had the doctor examine them and found that the defendants Wang Weixiang and Chen Ruilin both had caustic soda scars on their arms and faces, presumably because they were affected when they were pouring the caustic soda. Interrogated the defendants, whose confessions were evasive. Judge Wu Tingqi examined the confession and pronounced the judgment in court, sentencing Xu Liansheng to four years of imprisonment, Wang Weixiang and Zhang Huangguang to three years of imprisonment each, and the remaining Li, Chen, and Yang to six months of imprisonment each.

Case of British-Swiss Company Filing Charges for Selling Counterfeit Milk 162

Bao Maokun Released on Bail, Available for Summons

The head Westerner of the British-Swiss Condensed Milk Company recently discovered that inferior milk was being sold on the market, fraudulently using the company's Eagle Brand milk, at low prices. A detailed investigation revealed that Limin Company, located at 910 Avenue Edward VII, was selling this counterfeit milk. The method of counterfeiting involved Bao Maokun, the owner of Limin Company, purchasing Iron Anchor brand milk from the Lixin Foreign Firm on Peking Road for nineteen yuan per case. He would then remove the Iron Anchor trademark and label, replacing it with the Dapeng (Roc) brand. The Roc brand's logo also featured an eagle, making it difficult to distinguish at a glance due to the similarity between "eagle" and "roc." The selling price per case was increased by two yuan. However, genuine Eagle Brand milk cost twenty-six to twenty-seven taels of silver per case, while Bao only sold it for twenty-one yuan, severely impacting legitimate business. Therefore, the New Gate Police Station was informed, which in turn reported to the Special District Court. A search warrant was issued, and two days ago, Western Detective H. Ellis and Chinese Detective Gao Yanrong went to Limin Company and seized several thousand Dapeng Brand eagle trademark papers. These were taken to the police station and forwarded to the Special Court for instructions yesterday morning. The police station's lawyer, Wang Yaotang, presented the case, stating that the police station would file a separate lawsuit against Bao Maokun. Bao was already present, so he asked the court to review the evidence. Bao then stated that the milk sold by his company was Dapeng Brand, not Eagle Brand. After reviewing the evidence, Judge Wu Tingqi ordered Bao to be released on bail and available for summons, pending a rescheduled hearing.

Zhen Dan Fire Extinguisher Demonstrated in Zhabei Yesterday 165

The Jiqiu Brand foam fire extinguisher invented by the Zhen Dan Machinery Iron Factory at 363 Zhejiang Road has undergone repeated demonstrations with remarkable results. The factory, due to a large order from major merchants in Nanyang, will ship a large quantity to Singapore, Nanyang, and other places starting this week. Therefore, yesterday, a preliminary demonstration of the fire extinguisher's power was held at the Zhabei Charity Corps training ground. The Zhabei Fire Brigade was notified beforehand to avoid misunderstandings, and Chief Jin of the Fourth District of the Public Security Bureau was requested to send police officers to maintain order. A wooden frame was erected in the field, filled with wood. The demonstration began at 2 PM. First, a container of kerosene and gasoline was poured onto the grass and ignited. The foam was applied, and the fire was immediately extinguished. Then, items such as films were ignited, and they were also immediately extinguished. Next, three containers of kerosene and gasoline were poured onto the wooden frame and ignited. Flames and smoke billowed into the sky, making it impossible to approach. The fire's intensity reached its peak. The fire extinguisher was then used to spray the fire, and the flames were extinguished within just one minute. The audience applauded thunderously. The demonstration's success was highly satisfactory. It is said that the factory will conduct a large-scale demonstration at the public sports field in the Nanshi area, and all sectors will be invited to attend and observe.

Meeting Minutes of the Jixi Native Place Association 170

The Jixi Shanghai Native Place Association held its fourth joint executive and supervisory committee meeting yesterday. Shao Shuwei was elected chairman and Hu Peiru was the recorder. Meeting Minutes of the Rui Hua Fang Tenants Association 171

The Tenants Association of Rui Hua Fang on Route Pichon held a membership meeting yesterday. Zhu Yin was elected as the chairman after the meeting was convened. (1) The chairman reported on the progress: the landlord's side had been requested in writing on (the 10th) but had not responded. News from Various Labor Unions 173

Dockworkers' Union: Yesterday, the union convened a joint meeting of unions from districts one, two, four, and five to discuss the establishment of a general association for all docks. More than sixty foremen attended. Wu Jiaze presided over the meeting, and after the customary greetings, Zhou Funong gave a detailed guidance, hoping for cooperation between labor and foremen to benefit both sides forever. Then, the following were discussed separately: (1) The date for the establishment of the general association. It was resolved that the general association would be established immediately after the issuance of badges. (2) How to raise funds for the issuance of badges. It was resolved that each dock would temporarily contribute one month's fee, which was unanimously approved. (3) The method of issuing badges and collecting membership fees should follow the pricing set by the Municipal Party Headquarters. Who should be responsible for collecting fees at the docks? It was resolved that the dock foremen would be responsible for handling the accounts. However, before the badges are issued, the Party, government, military, and police agencies must issue a notice to protect these responsible persons.

Tailors' Union: The fourth executive committee meeting was held the night before last. Li Chengzhang presided over the meeting after the customary greetings. The following matters were discussed: (1) The case of workers from Hechangfu, Cao Shengji, and three other companies on Sichuan Road damaging union affairs. It was resolved to impose separate punishments. (2) Request to the Municipal Citizens' Training Association to revise the conditions. It was resolved to submit the request again and appoint a person to liaise. (3) Re-determination of staff salaries. It was resolved that the secretary would receive 40 yuan and the collectors would receive 30 yuan. (4) The collectors should submit daily payments. It was resolved that the collectors must submit the day's earnings to the union every night.

Monochrome Lithography Machine Association: The ninth regular meeting was held the day before yesterday. Zhou Yongfa presided over the meeting. The following were discussed: (1) The Wen Hua and Shi Xin bookstores laid off workers and stopped machines without reason. It was resolved to submit a request to the Municipal Citizens' Training Association and the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to handle the matter. (2) The Hui Wen Tang bookstore reduced the number of printing presses and canceled Lin Henian's five-cent wage. It was resolved to cancel it from October 15th. The meeting adjourned.

Acknowledgment: We received a complimentary copy each of the 26th volume, ninth and tenth issues of Children's World and the 773rd issue of the English Weekly from the Commercial Press yesterday. Thank you.
